    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">بَعَضَ</orth>
                  </form>,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَعُوض</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">gnats,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">musquitoes,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">bit him; and annoyed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">molested, him.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">بُعِضُوا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">They were bitten by the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَعُوض</foreign>: (A:) or <hi rend="ital">were annoyed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">molested, thereby.</hi> (K.) <foreign lang="ar">بَعَضَهُ</foreign> is not used in relation to anything but <foreign lang="ar">بَعُوض</foreign>. (TA.) A poet says, praising a man who passed the night within a <foreign lang="ar">كِلَّة</foreign> [or thin curtain used for protection from gnats, or musquitoes], which is also called <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو دِثَارٍ</foreign>, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَنِعْمَ البَيْتُ بَيْتُ أَبِى دِثَارٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا مَا خَافَ بَعْضُ القَوْمِ بَعْضَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Excellent indeed is the tent, the tent of Aboo-Dithár, when some of the people fear biting, and annoyance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">molestation, from gnats,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">musquitoes</hi>]: by <foreign lang="ar">بعضا</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">عَضًّا</foreign>. (TA.)    </entryFree>26:T6e8,<entryFree id="n2892" key="بعضهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بعضهُ</orth>

                  <hi rend="ital">They took his property and divided it into parts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portions.</hi> (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">عَضَّى الشَّاةَ وَ بَعَّضَهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He limbed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dismembered, the sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goat, and divided it into parts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portions</hi>]. (A, TA.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> in certain cases, and <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> in the like cases, as in the saying <foreign lang="ar">شَرِبْتُ بِمَآءِ كَذَا</foreign> [“ I drank of, ” i. e. “ some of, such water ”], are said to be <foreign lang="ar">لِلتَّبْعِيضِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">For the purpose of dividing into parts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portions</hi>]. (Msb.)    </entryFree>27:T17df,<entryFree id="n2895" key="بَعْضٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">عض</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بعض</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Some,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">somewhat</hi> or <hi rend="ital">some one,</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">a thing,</hi>) of things, or of a thing: Th says that it signifies thus accord. to all the grammarians; (Msb, TA;) except Hishám, as will be seen hereafter: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a part,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion,</hi> (A, Msb, K,) of a thing, (Msb,) or of anything; (A, K;) whether little or much: (TA:) accord. to both these explanations, it may denote the greater part; as eight of ten: (Msb:) [thus it signifies <hi rend="ital">some one</hi> or <hi rend="ital">more;</hi> and it relates to persons and to other things:] pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَبْعَاضٌ</foreign>; (S, IJ, K;) but ISd doubts whether IJ had an authority for this. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضُ الشَّرِّ أَهْوَنُ مِنْ بَعْضٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Some kinds of evil are easier to be borne than some</hi>]. (A.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَارِيَةٌ حُسَّانَةٌ يُشْبِهُ بَعْضُهَا بَعْضًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A very beautiful girl, parts of whom resemble other parts</hi>]. (A.) [And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ بَعْضُهُمْ بَعْضًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Some of them beat some;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">they beat one another.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">لَبِثْنَا يَوْمًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ بَعْضَ يَوْمٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">We have tarried a day or part of a day</hi>]. (Kur xviii. 18.) And one says to a man of a company of men, “ Who did this? ” and he answers, <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُنَا</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضُنَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Some one of us</hi>]; meaning himself. (A.) The article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> should not be prefixed to it, (K, * TA,) because it is originally a prefixed n., and as such determinate either literally or virtually, so that it does not admit another cause of being determinate; (TA;) contr. to what is said by IDrst (K, TA) and Ez-Zejjájee; for they said <foreign lang="ar">البَعْضُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الكُلُّ</foreign>; which, properly, as ISd says, is not allowable; and it is said in the O that IDrst, in this matter, was at variance with all the people of his age: (TA:) AHát says that the Arabs did not say <foreign lang="ar">الكُلُّ</foreign> nor <foreign lang="ar">البَعْضُ</foreign>, but that people used these expressions, even Sb and Akh in their two books, by reason of their little knowledge in this way: (K, * TA:) a remark, says MF, which is extr., and needs no comment: (TA:) [for who surpassed Sb and Akh in knowledge respecting matters of this kind?] AHát also relates his having told As that he had seen in the book of [that celebrated and chaste author] Ibn-ElMukaffa', <foreign lang="ar">العِلْمُ الكَثِيرٌ وَ لٰكِنَّ أَخْذَ البَعْضِ خَيْرٌ مِنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَرْكِ الكُلِّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Science is large; but the acquiring of part is better than the neglecting of the whole</hi>]; and that As disapproved of it most strongly, saying that the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> is not prefixed to <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كُلٌّ</foreign> because they are determinate without it: (TA:) Az, however, says that the grammarians allow its being prefixed to these two words, (Msb, TA,) though As disallows it, (TA,) because they are meant to be understood as prefixed ns.; (Msb;) or because the article is meant to be a substitute for the noun to which they should be prefixed; or, in the case of <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</foreign>, because this word is equivalent to <foreign lang="ar">جُزْءٌ</foreign>, which receives the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>. (MF.) It is related of AO, that he assigned also to <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</foreign> the contr. meaning of <hi rend="ital">All;</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">whole:</hi> adducing as a proof thereof the words of the Kur [xl. 29], <foreign lang="ar">يُصِبْكُمْ بَعْضُ ٱلَّذِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَعِدُكُمْ</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">All of that with which he threateneth you will befall you:</hi> and the saying of Lebeed. <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ يَعْتَلِقْ بَعْضَ النُّفُوسِ حِمَامُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">Or their death shall cling to all living creatures:</hi> or, accord. to another relation, <foreign lang="ar">او يَرْتَبِطْ</foreign>, which means the same as <foreign lang="ar">او يعتلق</foreign>]: thus also AHeyth explains the above-cited verse of the Kur; and thus Hishám explains the saying of Lebeed, erroneously asserting that <foreign lang="ar">بعض</foreign> is here a pl.: (TA:) but with respect to the former instance, the Prophet had threatened them with two things, the punishment of the present world and that of the world to come; so he says, “ This punishment will befall you in the present world; ” which is part (<foreign lang="ar">بعض</foreign>] of the two threats; without denying the punishment of the world to come: or, as Aboo-Is-hák says, he mentions the part to indicate the necessary consequence of the whole: and as to the saying of Lebeed, by <foreign lang="ar">بعض النفوس</foreign> he means himself. (TA [app. from ISd].)    </entryFree>28:T58e,<entryFree id="n2897" key="بَعُوضٌ" type="main">

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بَعُوضٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">عوض</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بعوض</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Gnats,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">musquitoes;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَقَّ</foreign> [which signifies both gnats, or musquitoes, (called in Egypt <foreign lang="ar">نَامُوس</foreign>,) and also bugs]: n. un. with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>: (S:) or pl. of <foreign lang="ar">بَعُوضَةٌ</foreign>, (K,) which signifies <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَقَّةٌ</foreign>. (A, K.) A poet speaks of the humming of the <foreign lang="ar">بعوض</foreign> of the water. (TA.) The author of the K says, in the B, that the word is taken from <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٌ</foreign>, because of the smallness of the body of the <foreign lang="ar">بعوضة</foreign> in comparison with other living things. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّفَنِى مُخَّ البَعُوضِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical> <hi rend="ital">He imposed upon me a difficult thing:</hi> (A:) or <hi rend="ital">an impossible thing.</hi> (TS, K.)    </entryFree>11:["$","$Lc",null,{"direction":"row","alignItems":"flex-start","width":"100%","background":"white","padding":{"base":"16px 8px","md":"24px 24px 32px
